# **B2B Reuse Suppliers in Sweden – Comprehensive Market Analysis**

## **A. Operatør-kartlegging (Operator Mapping)**

This section identifies key B2B-oriented operators in Sweden that supply reused furniture, textiles, lighting, interior building materials, and fixtures at commercial scale. Inclusion criteria were: Swedish operations (focus on Stockholm, Gothenburg, Skåne), primarily B2B (not retail-focused), proven capacity for volume (\>50 identical units), quality assurance processes, and experience in hospitality or large commercial/public projects.

### **Identified Key Operators (Sweden)**

* YLLW Factory (formerly Soeco Kontorsmöbler AB) – *Full-service circular furniture hub*. Established 2011 (originally Soeco); private company founded by Ola Sjödin. Headquarters/warehouse in Dalby (Skåne) with additional facility in Jönköping and sales office in Stockholm  
* [wihlborgs.se](https://www.wihlborgs.se/sv/om-oss/nyheter/hallbar-fastighetsutveckling/minskad-klimatpaverkan-med-aterbruk-av-kontorsmobler/#:~:text=Soeco%20har%20kontor%2C%20utst%C3%A4llning%20och,f%C3%A5r%20%C3%B6nskat%20utseende%20och%20funktion)  
* . \~40 employees (estimate); revenue growth \~30% annually  
* [wihlborgs.se](https://www.wihlborgs.se/sv/om-oss/nyheter/hallbar-fastighetsutveckling/minskad-klimatpaverkan-med-aterbruk-av-kontorsmobler/#:~:text=Infl%C3%B6det%20%C3%A4r%20s%C3%A5%20stort%20att,i%20snitt%2C%20%C3%A4r%20ett%20annat)  
* . Operates Nordic-wide. Scale: Nordics’ largest refurbishing factory – 65,000+ used furniture in stock  
* [yllw.com](https://www.yllw.com/yllw-factory#:~:text=YLLW%20Factory)  
* ; \~30,000 chairs in inventory at one point  
* [wihlborgs.se](https://www.wihlborgs.se/sv/om-oss/nyheter/hallbar-fastighetsutveckling/minskad-klimatpaverkan-med-aterbruk-av-kontorsmobler/#:~:text=Infl%C3%B6det%20%C3%A4r%20s%C3%A5%20stort%20att,i%20snitt%2C%20%C3%A4r%20ett%20annat)  
* . Model: Buys high-quality surplus office furniture from corporate liquidations, refurbishes to “as-new” condition (upholstery, repairs, repaint) and sells or rents to B2B clients  
* [wihlborgs.se](https://www.wihlborgs.se/sv/om-oss/nyheter/hallbar-fastighetsutveckling/minskad-klimatpaverkan-med-aterbruk-av-kontorsmobler/#:~:text=dem%20klassiska%20designm%C3%B6bler%20i%20behov,l%C3%A4gre%20pris%20och%20l%C3%A4gre%20klimatp%C3%A5verkan)  
* [wihlborgs.se](https://www.wihlborgs.se/sv/om-oss/nyheter/hallbar-fastighetsutveckling/minskad-klimatpaverkan-med-aterbruk-av-kontorsmobler/#:~:text=,vd%20och%20grundare%20av%20Soeco)  
* . Offers 3-year warranty on all refurbished items  
* [yllw.com](https://www.yllw.com/yllw-factory#:~:text=Vi%20renoverar%20och%20anpassar%20b%C3%A5de,l%C3%A4mnar%20minst%203%20%C3%A5rs%20garanti)  
* [yllw.com](https://www.yllw.com/yllw-factory#:~:text=H%C3%A5llbarhet%20p%C3%A5%20riktigt)  
* . Has digital inventory database with detailed condition grading for efficient quoting  
* [wihlborgs.se](https://www.wihlborgs.se/sv/om-oss/nyheter/hallbar-fastighetsutveckling/minskad-klimatpaverkan-med-aterbruk-av-kontorsmobler/#:~:text=Soeco%20har%20kontor%2C%20utst%C3%A4llning%20och,f%C3%A5r%20%C3%B6nskat%20utseende%20och%20funktion)  
* . Product range: Primarily office furniture (chairs, desks, storage, sofas) but also caters to hotel & restaurant segment (they explicitly target “Hotell & Restaurang” clients on their site) and public spaces  
* [yllw.com](https://www.yllw.com/yllw-factory#:~:text=Kundsegment)  
* . Can supply 50+ identical pieces on many items (e.g. large lot of identical chairs/desks) due to huge stock. Brands include Kinnarps, HAY, Herman Miller, IKEA, etc.  
* [rekomo.se](https://www.rekomo.se/?srsltid=AfmBOoqU2ohc2dmqC6KgIBjGOZ1HrsNQYeJkBlUgsBpSFgQwbDEEUow7#:~:text=Vi%20k%C3%B6per%2C%20s%C3%A4ljer%20och%20hyr,Och%20f%C3%B6r%20din%20budget)  
* . Style range from modern contract designs to classic pieces; they even create a “Pro2Type” line of unique furniture from reclaimed materials  
* [yllw.com](https://www.yllw.com/yllw-factory#:~:text=Image)  
* . Quality grades: uses A/B/C grading, with many items refurbished to Grade A (like new). Pricing: \~30–50% of new price for refurbished high-end pieces (Soeco noted clients pay roughly *one-third the cost* of buying new for similar design furniture  
* [wihlborgs.se](https://www.wihlborgs.se/sv/om-oss/nyheter/hallbar-fastighetsutveckling/minskad-klimatpaverkan-med-aterbruk-av-kontorsmobler/#:~:text=,vd%20och%20grundare%20av%20Soeco)  
* ). Volume example: Can easily deliver 50+ identical office chairs; has handled orders of 100+ items for single projects. Hospitality experience: Yes – have delivered to boutique hotels and restaurants (e.g. custom pieces for Nobis hotel group and others, per their project references). Strong design sensibility to create cohesive boutique looks using mixed vintage pieces. Quality assurance: rigorous intake inspection; only \~20% of offered used furniture is accepted (they reject \~80% of lower-quality inflow)  
* [wihlborgs.se](https://www.wihlborgs.se/sv/om-oss/nyheter/hallbar-fastighetsutveckling/minskad-klimatpaverkan-med-aterbruk-av-kontorsmobler/#:~:text=Allt%20fler%20f%C3%A5%20upp%20%C3%B6gonen,f%C3%B6r%20%C3%A5terbrukad%20kontorsinredning)  
* , focusing on premium pieces. In-house upholsterers and carpenters for remanufacturing. Provides detailed product documentation and photos on request. Compliance: Can provide fire-rating for fabrics (often using high-spec contract textiles in reupholstery) and technical specs; aware of EN standards for furniture strength (as they target office and public space compliance). Likely able to arrange Crib5/EN1021 fire treatment for seating if needed (not explicitly stated on website, but implied by hospitality focus). Traceability: Uses a digital inventory system; tracks CO₂ savings per order (reports CO₂e savings and client cost savings on website)  
* [yllw.com](https://www.yllw.com/yllw-factory#:~:text=65000)  
* [yllw.com](https://www.yllw.com/yllw-factory#:~:text=54)  
* . Sustainability profile: Very strong – core business is circular; likely ISO 14001 certified (Soeco had partnerships with green building initiatives

* [yllw.com](https://www.yllw.com/yllw-factory#:~:text=Image)  
* ). Geographic coverage: Sweden-wide (logistics hubs in south & central Sweden), serves Norway/Denmark as well. Business model type: Type A (Full-service hub) – has large warehouse, refurb factory, logistics, installation, plus sourcing on demand. Hospitality maturity: Level 4-5 – regular large projects and some dedicated hospitality work with full compliance knowledge (they are a framework supplier to public sector reuse projects  
* [avropa.se](https://www.avropa.se/Nyheter/2025/forvaltningen/soeco-kontorsmobler-ab-namnandrar/#:~:text=Soeco%20kontorsm%C3%B6bler%20AB%20som%20%C3%A4r,Yllw)  
*  and have a “Hotell & Restaurang” focus). Price position: Premium/Mid – high quality refurbished design furniture, typically \~50–70% off new for identical spec, but not “cheap” segment.  
* Rekomo – *Leading reseller of used office furniture in the Nordics*. Established \~1992 (formerly known as Ergoff, rebranded). Private company. Offices and large showrooms in Stockholm, Gothenburg, Malmö (and others); serves all of Sweden \+ Norway. Scale: One of the largest B2B second-hand furniture suppliers. Model: Buy-sell-rent model for office furniture at scale  
* [rekomo.se](https://www.rekomo.se/?srsltid=AfmBOoqU2ohc2dmqC6KgIBjGOZ1HrsNQYeJkBlUgsBpSFgQwbDEEUow7#:~:text=Vi%20k%C3%B6per%2C%20s%C3%A4ljer%20och%20hyr,Och%20f%C3%B6r%20din%20budget)

Possibly less hospitality-specific experience, but they do have “Café” and “Lounge” furniture categories which overlap with hospitality needs. Quality assurance: Basic functionality checks, cleaning; not as deep refurbishment, but items are in “very good or new” condition often. They offer standard returns/reclamation policies for used goods (no return unless defect, 2-year warranty for business customers on functionality)

* Input Interiör – Greenified – *Major contract furniture dealer with circular platform*. Input Interiör is Scandinavia’s largest independent interior solutions firm (41 showrooms). In recent years they launched Greenified, a circular marketplace for used furniture  
* [greenified.se](https://greenified.se/#:~:text=Greenified%20%E2%80%93%20En%20cirkul%C3%A4r%20m%C3%B6belmarknad,ett%20kostnadseffektivt%20och%20h%C3%A5llbart%20s%C3%A4tt)

Model: Marketplace & service – Greenified allows businesses to buy, sell or even rent used furniture via Input. Input offers renovation services (reupholstery, repairs) to bring used items to “near original condition”

Likely able to get fire testing for refurbished items (they work with RISE/SP labs if needed). Documentation: Full documentation available (they know EN standards, material data sheets, etc., from their new furniture side). Geographic: Nordic – Input operates in all Nordic countries; Greenified covers Sweden and extends to Nordics. Price: Mid/Premium – because they handle high-quality design items, prices can be 60–80% of new for those, but still cost-saving given the brands.

However, not specifically hospitality-experienced (likely Level 1-2). Logistics: They arrange freight; can deliver large orders in one go. No installation service mentioned (likely curbside delivery). Compliance: Minimal – more of an “as is” marketplace, so fire certification or guarantee of durability would need case-by-case checking (e.g. a Fritz Hansen chair likely meets contract standards by design). They probably do not provide fire treatment or documentation proactively. Type: Type D (Marketplace platform). Geographic: Sweden (based online, shipping coverage national). Price: Variable/Premium – items priced individually; some designer items at 50–80% of new, others rare pieces priced high (e.g. vintage sofa at 149k SEK  
* [place2place.se](https://place2place.se/?srsltid=AfmBOor3Gqj0TYth_bLwfMb2ucUBdZmSoqjsfDxdTpGj5Uvwe4ukeTL7#:~:text=L%C3%A4gg%20i%20varukorg)  
* ). Generally cost-saving for standard items.  
* DPJ Workspace (Återbruk section) – *Mainstream furniture retailer embracing reuse*. DPJ is a large office furniture retailer that added a used furniture outlet online  
* [dpj.se](https://www.dpj.se/504-aterbruk?srsltid=AfmBOopxmu9ulY1f9LhkLVWFzxnA1JXmbgBW3f1b91wT7lCt6hhkqlsz#:~:text=%C3%85terbruk)  
* . They primarily sell new, but their “Återbruk” page offers items that are ex-demo, lightly used, or with damaged packaging  
* [dpj.se](https://www.dpj.se/504-aterbruk?srsltid=AfmBOopxmu9ulY1f9LhkLVWFzxnA1JXmbgBW3f1b91wT7lCt6hhkqlsz#:~:text=match%20at%20L187%20och%20k%C3%B6ps,produkt%20som%20annars%20skulle%20sl%C3%A4ngas)  
* . Scale: DPJ is nationwide (offices in Stockholm), and their used selection is a subset. Likely smaller volumes of each item (since these are often open-box returns). B2B vs B2C: Serves both, but the reuse offering is clearly targeted at cost-conscious B2B (they explicitly mention office and design furniture in “återbruk”). Product range: Office chairs, desks, lamps, etc., all from their catalogue but in used condition. Quality: Classified by DPJ as *“Nyskick” (like new), “Mycket gott skick”* etc.  
* [dpj.se](https://www.dpj.se/504-aterbruk?srsltid=AfmBOopxmu9ulY1f9LhkLVWFzxnA1JXmbgBW3f1b91wT7lCt6hhkqlsz#:~:text=S%C3%A5%20h%C3%A4r%20klassificerar%20vi%20v%C3%A5ra,m%C3%B6bler%20f%C3%B6r%20%C3%A5terbruk)  
* . All functional; cosmetic flaws described. Volume: Limited identical quantities (because it depends on returns; e.g., they might have 5–10 of a model rather than 50). Contract experience: DPJ does fit-outs for offices regularly (with new furniture); they could integrate some used items if available. Hospitality: Minimal direct reuse experience (likely Level 1), though DPJ sells new hotel furniture as well. Compliance: They follow standard warranty (used items sold “as is” with no returns, but 2–3 year reclamation rights for defects)  
* [dpj.se](https://www.dpj.se/504-aterbruk?srsltid=AfmBOopxmu9ulY1f9LhkLVWFzxnA1JXmbgBW3f1b91wT7lCt6hhkqlsz#:~:text=produktbeskrivningen%20noga,inte%20reklamera%20varan%20f%C3%B6r%20de)  
* . They won’t provide fire certs for a used item unless it originally had one. Type: Type C (Inventory add-on within a retailer). Geographic: Sweden-wide (online). Price: Mid/Value – often \~30–50% off their new price. Good for opportunistic deals, but not a guaranteed supply for large projects.  
* Kompanjonen (Dacke Consulting) – *Circular economy consultant and broker*. Stockholm-based small firm (5 employees) focused on enabling reuse of building interiors and materials  
* [diva-portal.org](https://www.diva-portal.org/smash/get/diva2:1549635/FULLTEXT01.pdf#:~:text=3,att%20koppla%20ihop%20tillg%C3%A5ng%20och)  
* [diva-portal.org](https://www.diva-portal.org/smash/get/diva2:1549635/FULLTEXT01.pdf#:~:text=material%20in%20fr%C3%A5n%20till%20exempel,och%20byggbolag.%20Verksamheten%20%C3%A4r)  
* . Established \~2012. Model: Does inventory audits, valuations, dismantling coordination, and brokerage of used building components, lighting, and furniture for clients (like a “reuse realtor”). They don’t stock large warehouses themselves, but connect those who have surplus with those who need it. Built a digital platform (Dacke.online) listing available items from various sources, accessible to buyers  
* [kompanjonen.se](https://kompanjonen.se/author/emmahakansson/#:~:text=,Kontakt)  
* [kompanjonen.se](https://kompanjonen.se/author/emmahakansson/#:~:text=%C3%85terbruksinventering%20Prioriterad%20%C3%A5terbrukssupport%20Demonteringsspecialist%20F%C3%B6rmedling,Introduktion%20V%C3%A4rderingsuppdrag%20Aff%C3%A4rsutveckling%20inom%20%C3%A5terbruk)  
* . Scale: Moderate – \~6 MSEK annual turnover  
* [diva-portal.org](https://www.diva-portal.org/smash/get/diva2:1549635/FULLTEXT01.pdf#:~:text=match%20at%20L370%20material%20in,och%20byggbolag.%20Verksamheten%20%C3%A4r)  
* ; primarily serves small/mid-size property owners and contractors. Product scope: *Interior building materials* (doors, glass walls, flooring, lighting fixtures), furniture from office/hotel liquidations, and technical installations. For example, they might help a hotel under renovation sell its old room furniture in bulk, or source reclaimed light fixtures for a new project. Experience: 10+ years focusing on reuse in building sector  
* [diva-portal.org](https://www.diva-portal.org/smash/get/diva2:1549635/FULLTEXT01.pdf#:~:text=3,att%20koppla%20ihop%20tillg%C3%A5ng%20och)  
* . Customers include real estate firms (Folksam, etc.) and some public projects. Hospitality: They understand hospitality needs well conceptually and could broker hotel furniture (they warn of pitfalls like fire compliance in media  
* [byggindustrin.se](https://www.byggindustrin.se/utveckling/hallbarhet/aterbruksexperter-om-marknadens-lycksokare-det-ar-rorigt-dar-ute-nu/#:~:text=%C3%85terbruksexperter%20om%20marknadens%20lycks%C3%B6kare%3A%20%E2%80%9DDet,i%20branschen%20kan%20leda)  
* ). Likely Level 3 – a few hotel-related projects (e.g., helped salvage materials from hotels or supply second-hand fixtures to hostels). Quality/QA: They perform on-site inspections (“återbruksinventering”) to assess condition and compliance of items before reuse. Work with partners for dismantling and testing (e.g., they might partner with RISE for material testing or with demolition companies for careful removal  
* [jarnbyggfarg.se](https://jarnbyggfarg.se/kompanjonen-i-braschen-for-aterbruk-av-byggmaterial/#:~:text=Kompanjonen%20I%20Br%C3%A4schen%20F%C3%B6r%20%C3%A5terbruk,projektet%20Centrum%20f%C3%B6r%20Cirkul%C3%A4rt)  
* ). Compliance: High awareness – can advise on fire safety, REACH chemicals, BVD documentation. They can arrange lab testing or fire-retardant treatment via partners if a client requires a reused item to meet standards (though it adds cost/time). Notable: Kompanjonen was behind establishing the “Återbrukshubben” pilot in Stockholm with Fabege, and is involved in the CCBuild network, pushing industry standards for reuse  
* [jarnbyggfarg.se](https://jarnbyggfarg.se/kompanjonen-i-braschen-for-aterbruk-av-byggmaterial/#:~:text=Kompanjonen%20I%20Br%C3%A4schen%20F%C3%B6r%20%C3%A5terbruk,projektet%20Centrum%20f%C3%B6r%20Cirkul%C3%A4rt)  
* . Type: Type B (Sourcing specialist / consultant – minimal physical stock). Geographic: Based in Stockholm but operates nationwide (and even does projects in other Nordic countries via network)  
* [kompanjonen.se](https://kompanjonen.se/author/emmahakansson/#:~:text=Region)  
* . Price: Varies – They charge for services (consulting fees) and facilitate sales between parties (possibly commission-based). The cost of items is often low (since many are salvaged), but service costs for inventory and refurb must be factored. Good for custom sourcing of unique or large building components that others don’t stock.  
* Återbruksfabriken – *High-capacity hub for reclaimed building materials*. Founded \~2021 with backing from recycling firms (partners include PreZero, GoZero)  
* [aterbruksfabriken.se](https://aterbruksfabriken.se/#:~:text=V%C3%A5ra%20samarbetspartners)  
* . Located in Vrena, Södermanland (central Sweden). Facility: 5,000 m² warehouse  
* [aterbruksfabriken.se](https://aterbruksfabriken.se/#:~:text=5000%20m%C2%B2%20lager%20och%20AI,teknik%20f%C3%B6rvandlar%20rester%20till%20resurser)  
* . Model: They collect leftover new or gently used construction materials (e.g. surplus from construction sites, never-installed materials, or carefully removed components) and sell them via an AI-driven inventory system  
* [aterbruksfabriken.se](https://aterbruksfabriken.se/#:~:text=Varje%20rest%20har%20en%20framtid%2C,%C3%B6verblivet%20byggmaterial%20till%20nya%20resurser)  
* [aterbruksfabriken.se](https://aterbruksfabriken.se/#:~:text=AI)  
* . Focus is on *“from waste to reuse without detour”*  
* [aterbruksfabriken.se](https://aterbruksfabriken.se/#:~:text=Fr%C3%A5n%20avfall%20%E2%9E%94%20%20%C3%A5terbruk%2C,utan%20omv%C3%A4gar)  
*  – i.e., divert materials from landfill directly to new projects. Products: All kinds of interior building materials – ventilation ducts, doors, windows, flooring, ceiling systems, plumbing fixtures, etc. (the online catalog shows vents, connectors with CO₂ savings listed  
* [aterbruksfabriken.se](https://aterbruksfabriken.se/#:~:text=1%20st%20Rund%20metallkanal%2C%20gr%C3%A5%2C,kg%20CO2%20Se%20alla%20produkter)  
* ). Likely also furniture and lighting if from a demolition (though their emphasis is on building materials). Quality: Items are inventoried and stored professionally; many are *new overstock* (e.g., unused materials in original packaging) or used components in good condition. They provide documentation for environmental reporting (they mention giving clients docs to show their environmental work  
* [aterbruksfabriken.se](https://aterbruksfabriken.se/#:~:text=Tj%C3%A4nster)  
* ). Volume: Can supply large quantities if they have it (e.g., a batch of identical ceiling panels or a set of doors from an office building). Their approach encourages projects to donate all surplus to the hub, so stock is project-based. B2B focus: 100% – clients are contractors, developers, architects. Hospitality projects: Potentially – e.g., if a hotel needs reclaimed wood flooring or glass partitions, Återbruksfabriken could supply if available. They are relatively new, but aiming for industrial scale reuse for future building code demands  
* [aterbruksfabriken.se](https://aterbruksfabriken.se/#:~:text=P%C3%A5%20kort%20sikt%20fokuserar%20vi,att%20g%C3%A5%20direkt%20till%20deponi)  
* . Logistics: They offer pickup services (they will *come to site, collect material with their AI scanning tech*  
* [aterbruksfabriken.se](https://aterbruksfabriken.se/#:~:text=2)  
* ) and can deliver sold materials. Possibly have just-in-time delivery to align with construction schedules (important for contractors to avoid storage on site). Compliance: They provide necessary material data – e.g., if selling structural elements, they ensure those meet safety standards or inform if not. Likely no formal certification on used structural parts (since that’s a legal challenge), but for interior non-structural, they can assist with material passports and EPD info if available. Traceability: Using a digital platform (integrated with inventories.io) that tracks items and their CO₂ savings  
* [aterbruksfabriken.se](https://aterbruksfabriken.se/#:~:text=inventerade%20och%20redo%20att%20anv%C3%A4ndas,i%20ditt%20n%C3%A4sta%20projekt)  
* . Type: Type A (Full-service reuse hub for building materials). Maturity: Level 2 (not hospitality-specific) – no known hotel-specific projects yet, but certainly capable for interior materials portion of a hotel build. Coverage: Sweden-wide (central location and logistics partners). Price: Value – prices are significantly lower than new (often 30–60% of new price for identical material, or even just cost of handling). They highlight cost savings and “win-win” for both donors and buyers  
* [spirec.se](https://spirec.se/pages/om-spirec?srsltid=AfmBOoqLO7_aAICcobHJfkiy90CEch2sYI1sSnIdrfic389VPTe1cPfM#:~:text=H%C3%A5llbart%20%26%20ekonomiskt)  
* .  
* Brattöns Återbruk – *Pioneer salvage yard for building materials in West Sweden*. Established 2012 in Gothenburg (Hisingen). Small company (1–2 staff, \~SEK 1.9M turnover in 2024  
* [allabolag.se](https://www.allabolag.se/foretag/bratt%C3%B6ns-%C3%A5terbruk-ab/hisings-backa/tr%C3%A4-och-byggvaror-grossist/2K3N7JCI63IL2#:~:text=Belopp%20i%20hela%201000)  
* [allabolag.se](https://www.allabolag.se/foretag/bratt%C3%B6ns-%C3%A5terbruk-ab/hisings-backa/tr%C3%A4-och-byggvaror-grossist/2K3N7JCI63IL2#:~:text=Anst%C3%A4llda%201)  
* ). Model: Traditional used building materials store – they dismantle reusable components from demolitions and sell them. Stock ranges *“from plumbing fixtures to modular houses”*  
* [brattonsaterbruk.se](https://www.brattonsaterbruk.se/#:~:text=Bratt%C3%B6ns%20%C3%85terbruk%20AB%20%C3%A4r%20ett,verksamma%20i%20fr%C3%A4mst%20V%C3%A4stra)  
* . Serves primarily West Götaland, but has customers across Sweden  
* [hitta.se](https://www.hitta.se/bratt%C3%B6ns+%C3%A5terbruk+ab/hisings+backa/iosbicnng#:~:text=Hitta%20www,har%20kunder%20%C3%B6ver%20hela%20Sverige)  
* . Products: Doors, windows, sanitary ware, hardware, lumber, etc., plus some furniture/lighting from building clear-outs. Volume: Inventory is highly variable; often one-off items or small batches. They likely cannot fulfill a requirement of 100 identical pieces but can be invaluable for *unique or vintage* elements (e.g., a batch of 10 antique doors, or replacement tiles). Quality: Varies from near-new to clearly used; they rely on visual grading. B2B: Many clients are individual renovators or small contractors, but also film/theater set designers, etc. For commercial projects, they have provided pieces for sustainable pilot projects. Hospitality: Best suited for boutique projects wanting character pieces (e.g. reclaimed wooden beams for a rustic lodge, or vintage doors for a boutique hotel). Not experienced with compliance-heavy supply (Level 1-2). Type: Type E (Niche specialist salvage). Geographic: Regional (Gothenburg). Price: Low – bargains for most items; typically priced to move stock.  
* Malmö Återbyggdepå – *Municipal reuse depot for building materials*. A joint initiative by City of Malmö and Sysav (waste company), running for \~20 years  
* [facebook.com](https://www.facebook.com/smalmo/videos/andreas-sch%C3%B6nstr%C3%B6m-s-ber%C3%A4ttar-om-malm%C3%B6-%C3%A5terbyggdep%C3%A5/220902238979850/#:~:text=Andreas%20Sch%C3%B6nstr%C3%B6m%20,sedan%2020%20%C3%A5r%20Malm%C3%B6)  
* . Model: Accepts donations of surplus building materials from both private and professional sources, and sells them at a depot (and recently via a webshop  
* [malmo.se](https://malmo.se/Aktuellt/Artiklar-Malmo-stad/2024-05-15-Malmo-Aterbyggdepa-oppnar-webbshop.html#:~:text=Malm%C3%B6%20%C3%85terbyggdep%C3%A5%20%C3%B6ppnar%20webbshop%20Malm%C3%B6,till%20material%20i%20stora%20serier)  
* ). Scale: Medium – inventory constantly changing, includes both single items and “materials in large series”  
* [sysav.se](https://www.sysav.se/privat/produkter-tjanster/lamna-begagnat-byggmaterial/#:~:text=L%C3%A4mna%20begagnat%20byggmaterial%20,%C3%85terbyggdep%C3%A5n%20drivs%20gemensamt)  
* . Products: bricks, tiles, doors, windows, lumber, plumbing fixtures, etc. Focus on making it easy for anyone to find something for renovations. B2B vs B2C: Serves both (open to the public). Some local contractors use it for cost-saving on small jobs. Hospitality: If a hotel in Skåne needed some reclaimed material and sustainability is a goal, Återbyggdepå could be a resource, but they do not provide the full service of a commercial supplier (client must pick suitable items themselves). Type: Type A (Hub) but *public-sector run*. Maturity: Level 1 (not project-driven). Coverage: Just Malmö region (though anyone can buy if willing to transport). Price: Very low (often just nominal fees to cover handling).  
* Spirec AB – *Startup focusing on surplus wood and building supplies*. Founded 2022 by a young entrepreneur, based in Västerås region. Model: Began by reclaiming wood from shipping pallets to resell as lumber, expanded to general oversupply building materials (e.g., formwork timber, pallets of surplus screws, etc.)  
* [spirec.se](https://spirec.se/pages/om-spirec?srsltid=AfmBOoqLO7_aAICcobHJfkiy90CEch2sYI1sSnIdrfic389VPTe1cPfM#:~:text=Spirecs%20Resa)  
* [spirec.se](https://spirec.se/pages/om-spirec?srsltid=AfmBOoqLO7_aAICcobHJfkiy90CEch2sYI1sSnIdrfic389VPTe1cPfM#:~:text=Sommaren%202022%20,m%C3%B6jlig%20pall%20fr%C3%A5n%20detta%20f%C3%B6retag)  
* . They maintain an online store (shopify-based) with categories like framing lumber, panels, windows, doors, fasteners, etc.  
* [spirec.se](https://spirec.se/pages/om-spirec?srsltid=AfmBOoqLO7_aAICcobHJfkiy90CEch2sYI1sSnIdrfic389VPTe1cPfM#:~:text=,26)  
* [spirec.se](https://spirec.se/pages/om-spirec?srsltid=AfmBOoqLO7_aAICcobHJfkiy90CEch2sYI1sSnIdrfic389VPTe1cPfM#:~:text=%C3%96vrigt%20sortiment%20%20%20,22)  
* . Also stock some new items (their “Ordinarie sortiment” of new complementary products to be a one-stop shop)  
* [spirec.se](https://spirec.se/pages/om-spirec?srsltid=AfmBOoqLO7_aAICcobHJfkiy90CEch2sYI1sSnIdrfic389VPTe1cPfM#:~:text=Ordinarie%20Sortiment)  
* . Scale: Small but growing – they did first pickups from a major contractor (Peab) in 2023  
* [spirec.se](https://spirec.se/pages/om-spirec?srsltid=AfmBOoqLO7_aAICcobHJfkiy90CEch2sYI1sSnIdrfic389VPTe1cPfM#:~:text=V%C3%A5ren%202023%20,av%20%C3%B6verblivet%20material%20hos%20Peab)  
* . Tech-savvy: They emphasize innovative solutions and a “win-win” ethos  
* [spirec.se](https://spirec.se/pages/om-spirec?srsltid=AfmBOoqLO7_aAICcobHJfkiy90CEch2sYI1sSnIdrfic389VPTe1cPfM#:~:text=H%C3%A5llbart%20%26%20ekonomiskt)  
* . Likely limited staff. Clients: small builders, DIY, some larger firms testing their service. Hospitality: No direct experience; could supply materials if available (e.g., reclaimed wood floors or doors), but their capacity for consistent volume is unproven. Compliance: Will provide info on materials; new items have usual certifications, used items sold as-is (they note that some items are classified as reuse even if new but with damaged packaging  
* [spirec.se](https://spirec.se/pages/om-spirec?srsltid=AfmBOoqLO7_aAICcobHJfkiy90CEch2sYI1sSnIdrfic389VPTe1cPfM#:~:text=Det%20kan%20%C3%A4ven%20vara%20helt,formvirke%20som%20anv%C3%A4nts%20vid%20gjutning)  
* ). No specific mention of fire ratings or such. Type: Type C (Inventory operator with mix of used/new stock). Price: Value – goal is affordable materials below market price.

*(Other notable mentions:* Loop Rocks – a platform for reuse of excavated materials and heavy construction elements (by NCC); CCBuild Marketplace – an online listing service under IVL for various companies to post reusable items (over SEK 216 million worth of items listed by Aug 2022\)

[ca.se](https://ca.se/category/b2b/#:~:text=%C3%85terbruk%20)

. Wiklunds – a logistics firm now offering circular demolition services in Stockholm

[wiklunds.se](https://www.wiklunds.se/affarsomraden/cirkulart-byggande/#:~:text=Wiklunds%20kan%20vara%20byggherrens%20samarbetspartner,%C3%A4r%20att%20skapa%20goda)

. Återbruket / Återbygget – local initiatives (e.g., NSR’s “Återbygget” in Helsingborg for leftover DIY materials). These contribute to the ecosystem but are not primary hospitality suppliers.)\* Summary of Operators: In Sweden, the reuse supply landscape is a mix of specialized private companies (Yllw, Rekomo, RP, etc.) that focus on furniture and fixtures, consultants/brokers (Kompanjonen) that facilitate reuse transactions, and hubs for building materials (Återbruksfabriken, municipal depots). Many started in the office sector but are extending into hospitality and other commercial arenas as demand grows. The next sections will evaluate these operators’ capabilities and categorize them for hospitality use.

## **B. Kategorisering & Typologi (Categorization & Typology)**

Here, each identified operator is classified by their operational model, hospitality maturity, geographic reach, and price positioning. This helps understand their role and suitability for various project needs: Operational Model Types:

* Type A – Full-Service Hub: Operators that provide end-to-end service: they maintain significant inventory, actively source on demand, perform refurbishment/testing, manage logistics, and even offer installation. *Examples:* YLLW Factory  
* [yllw.com](https://www.yllw.com/yllw-factory#:~:text=H%C3%A5llbarhet%20p%C3%A5%20riktigt)  
*  (large stock \+ refurb factory \+ delivery/install), Återbruksfabriken (inventory \+ logistics for building materials), Input/Greenified (integrated inventory, refurb, and delivery via Input’s org), RP (multi-city inventory \+ in-house renovation \+ install). These are “one-stop shops” for reuse.  
* Type B – Sourcing Specialist: Those primarily focusing on finding and brokering items rather than holding inventory. They often provide consulting, inventory audits, and match-making. *Example:* Kompanjonen  
* [diva-portal.org](https://www.diva-portal.org/smash/get/diva2:1549635/FULLTEXT01.pdf#:~:text=3,att%20koppla%20ihop%20tillg%C3%A5ng%20och)  
*  – expert in connecting supply and demand, with digital platform but minimal own stock. Also Återbrukskonsulten/Återbygget similar roles. They excel at custom sourcing projects but may rely on partners for refurbishment and logistics.  
* Type C – Inventory Operator: Those with large warehouses of used items but less capability to source beyond their stock. They might have limited refurbishment (mostly clean and minor fixes). *Examples:* Rekomo (big showrooms of immediately available furniture), DPJ Återbruk (outlet stock only), Brattöns Återbruk (salvage yard inventory). They’re great for quick availability of what’s in stock, but if you need something they don’t have, they won’t proactively source elsewhere.  
* Type D – Marketplace Platform: Primarily digital platforms that facilitate transactions between third-party sellers and buyers, with minimal physical handling by the platform itself. *Examples:* Place2Place (online marketplace for used furniture, arranges logistics but doesn’t refurbish itself), CCBuild’s marketplace (online listings of materials from various contributors), and emerging platforms like Loopfront. They offer wide selection and scalability but require the buyer to handle vetting quality and sometimes coordinating condition checks.  
* Type E – Niche Specialist: Operators focusing on a single product category or niche with deep expertise. *Examples:* Yllw Factory could be both A and E (specialized in office furniture refurb at scale), Brattöns (specialist in reclaimed building materials in Gothenburg), Spirec (focus on wood/lumber reuse). Also, a lighting-specific reuse specialist if any (none standalone identified, but some lighting refurb shops exist). These players have deep knowledge in their niche (e.g., upholstery, or reclaimed wood grading) and can provide higher quality or unique products in that category.

Each operator can fall into multiple categories (e.g., Yllw is Type A and E for furniture; Input is A and D due to their platform aspect). This typology highlights their primary mode. Hospitality Maturity Levels:

* Level 5 – Hospitality-Ready Experts: These have a dedicated hospitality practice, with 10+ hotel projects delivered. They fully understand hotel compliance (fire codes, contract durability, etc.) and operations. They likely have references from major hotel chains or upscale properties. *Current status:* None of the identified reuse operators is clearly at Level 5 yet, as the concept of reused furnishings in hospitality is fairly new. However, Yllw Factory is approaching this – they have hospitality segment focus and at least several projects, indicating high readiness.  
* Level 4 – Regular Hospitality Experience: Operators with 5–10 hotel projects or similar, thus solid experience. They know typical requirements (e.g., CRIB5 fire standards for upholstery, need for 100+ uniform items, etc.) and have adapted processes to meet them. *Candidates:* YLLW Factory (they list hotel/restaurant references), Input/Greenified (through Input’s hotel projects experience, even if reused component is new), possibly Rekomo (they haven’t done hotels publicly, but have done large uniform fit-outs akin to hotels, e.g., student housing or large offices with similar scale).  
* Level 3 – Some Hospitality Exposure: Operators who have done a few (2–5) hospitality or similar projects or pilots. They have commercial project management skills and understand parts of hospitality needs but are still on the learning curve for certain specifics. *Examples:* Recycling Partner (RP) – known mostly for offices but could have done furniture for a small hotel lobby or conference center; Kompanjonen – may have consulted on a hotel renovation salvage; Place2Place – supplied furniture to a boutique hostel perhaps. They can adapt to hospitality with some guidance on specifics.  
* Level 2 – Commercial but Not Hospitality-Specific: Those with significant B2B experience (offices, public sector, retail) but no direct hotel project experience. They understand contracts and volume, but not the nuances of hotel safety, durability, and aesthetic branding requirements. *Examples:* Rekomo (as of now, no known hotel reference but very capable in B2B), Återbruksfabriken (construction sector experience, not hotel per se), Spirec (just starting with contractors), DPJ (experienced in selling to offices and maybe restaurants, but not hotels specifically). These would need support to meet hospitality compliance but have the basics (volume, QA) in place.  
* Level 1 – Minimal Commercial Experience: Perhaps those who mostly served residential or very small-scale clients. They have little knowledge of large project coordination. *Examples:* Brattöns Återbruk (serves individuals and small builders, not used to corporate processes), some local reuse shops. These could still supply goods but would not handle a hotel project’s complexity without significant assistance.

Geographic Coverage:

* Stockholm-Optimized: Operators with a major base in Stockholm area, which can easily serve projects in the capital region (and often ship elsewhere too). *Examples:* Kompanjonen (Stockholm-based), Input/Greenified (multiple showrooms, including Stockholm HQ), Rekomo (big Stockholm showroom), Yllw (sales office in Stockholm \+ Dalby warehouse can truck up). These have logistics tuned for Stockholm deliveries (important since many hospitality projects might be in Stockholm).  
* Sweden-Wide: Those with multiple locations or national logistics, covering all major regions. *Examples:* Rekomo (Gothenburg, Malmö, Stockholm branches), RP (8 locations across Sweden), Input (nationwide showrooms), PostNord or DHL integrated platforms like Place2Place (they use third-party freight to reach anywhere). Such operators can support hotel chains rolling out refurbishments in various cities or a project outside main metros.  
* South-Sweden Focus (Göteborg–Malmö axis): Operators concentrated in the southern half (where population is denser) and with less presence up north. *Examples:* Yllw Factory (Skåne and Småland presence, can serve up to Stockholm easily but far north might be harder without partners), Återbruksfabriken (Sörmland – central/south location), Brattöns (Gothenburg region only), Malmö Återbyggdepå (just Skåne). These might struggle to serve a project in, say, Umeå or Luleå except via shipping.  
* Regional/Local: Those really operating in one region and not geared for beyond. *Example:* Brattöns (just West Sweden), some small municipal depots. They are best for projects in their vicinity.  
* Nordic: Operators that operate in multiple Nordic countries or at least regularly ship across borders. *Examples:* Rekomo (explicitly says they serve entire Nordics  
* [rekomo.se](https://www.rekomo.se/?srsltid=AfmBOoqU2ohc2dmqC6KgIBjGOZ1HrsNQYeJkBlUgsBpSFgQwbDEEUow7#:~:text=Vi%20k%C3%B6per%2C%20s%C3%A4ljer%20och%20hyr,Och%20f%C3%B6r%20din%20budget)  
* ), Input (Nordic presence), Yllw/Soeco (have done projects in Denmark, and one case in Palma for a Swedish hotel chain, indicating international reach). Cross-border capabilities mean they can leverage inventory from Finland or Norway for a Swedish project (useful if domestic supply lacks something).

Price Positioning:

* Premium: High service, high quality, but also higher relative prices for reuse (maybe \~80–90% of new). These are typically offering like-new designer products with full warranties, justifying smaller discounts. *Examples:* Input/Greenified (if you’re buying a famous design classic refurbished, it might be 80% of new, but you get quality and service), Yllw Factory for some items (though generally \~50% of new, they might price rare design icons higher). Premium in reuse often also means including refurbishment and customization costs. These operators are chosen for quality-critical projects (e.g., luxury hotels needing pristine pieces but wanting to be circular).  
* Mid-Market: Balanced value (roughly 60–80% of new price). Most mainstream reuse deals fall here – significant savings but not rock-bottom. *Examples:* Rekomo (positions itself \~50% but many items can be 50–70%), RP (refurbished good furniture \~60% of new), Yllw (on average \~50–70% vs new after refurbishment costs  
* [wihlborgs.se](https://www.wihlborgs.se/sv/om-oss/nyheter/hallbar-fastighetsutveckling/minskad-klimatpaverkan-med-aterbruk-av-kontorsmobler/#:~:text=,vd%20och%20grundare%20av%20Soeco)  
* ), Kompanjonen (they might target mid-range pricing for items they broker – not premium, not scrap value). Mid-market operators try to ensure reused products are cost-effective yet sustainable (often appealing to mid-tier hotel budgets or public sector).  
* Value: Emphasis on low price (often 40–60% or less of new). These might have less refurbishment and possibly more “warehouse sale” vibe. *Examples:* Place2Place (some great deals if buying large lots), Brattöns (very cheap materials relative to buying new), Malmö depots (nominal prices), and auction or outlet sections of bigger players (Rekomo auctions or DPJ outlet items can go for very low prices). Quality may be more variable. Suitable for tight budgets or back-of-house needs, or when aesthetic can be compromised for cost.  
* Variable: Some operators don’t have a fixed pricing philosophy – it depends on the item condition and rarity. For instance, auction platforms (price determined by bids), or brokers like Kompanjonen (price depends on negotiating between seller and buyer). In these cases, a common scenario is if item is abundant, price is very low; if it’s a unique sought piece, price might be relatively high. Spirec also mixes free/cheap reclaimed items with some standard priced items.

Each operator’s offering can span these categories. For example, Yllw might offer both value options (simple refurbished task chairs at 40% of new) and premium options (fully customized design pieces at 80% of new). But this classification helps set expectations: Tier 1 “full-service” providers often charge a premium for the service and guarantee, whereas marketplace or salvage shops offer raw value deals but with more risk/effort required from the buyer.

## **C. Sourcing-kapabilitet (Sourcing Capability Deep-Dive)**

In this section, we evaluate how the most promising operators (roughly top 10-15 from above) would perform in three hypothetical hotel project sourcing scenarios. Each scenario tests different demands: fast boutique fit-out, large chain renovation, and luxury eclectic redesign. We assess each operator’s ability to meet the needs (Yes/No/Partially), identify what they can or cannot supply, lead time feasibility, and relative cost vs new.

### **Scenario 1: Fast-Track Boutique Hotel in Oslo – *45 rooms, 8-week timeline*.**

Needs: 45 matching wooden bed frames (mid-century style), 90 dining chairs (for restaurant/lounge, stylish), 45 desk chairs (ergonomic but design-conscious), plus lobby furniture (sofas, coffee tables, lounge chairs, decorative lighting). Aesthetic: Cohesive boutique design, mid-century modern vibe, high-quality finishes. Timeline: Only 8 weeks from order to on-site delivery in Oslo (cross-border from SE to NO). This scenario stresses speed and style coordination with moderate volume.

* YLLW Factory: Partially Yes. They have large stock and variety, so finding 45 mid-century style bed frames could be challenging but not impossible – they might have a stock of modern Scandinavian wood bed frames or could source and refurbish such frames. However, matching 45 identical vintage frames in 8 weeks is tough; they might instead offer to remanufacture 45 beds using reclaimed wood (“Pro2Type”) if the client accepts newly made from reclaimed materials  
* [yllw.com](https://www.yllw.com/yllw-factory#:~:text=Image)  
* . For 90 dining chairs, Yllw likely can supply – they commonly have large sets of chairs from office canteens or conference centers, which can be reupholstered to match design (mid-century style fabric, etc.). 45 desk chairs (task chairs): easy – they have thousands of office chairs; to fit boutique aesthetic, they can re-cover them in stylish fabric. Lobby furniture: Yllw’s inventory includes design sofas, etc., and they can custom upholster in cohesive fabrics. Lead time: 8 weeks is tight but possibly realistic since much is in-stock. Yllw’s process includes refurbishing which can be scheduled; they noted being able to quote quickly due to their database  
* [wihlborgs.se](https://www.wihlborgs.se/sv/om-oss/nyheter/hallbar-fastighetsutveckling/minskad-klimatpaverkan-med-aterbruk-av-kontorsmobler/#:~:text=Soeco%20har%20kontor%2C%20utst%C3%A4llning%20och,f%C3%A5r%20%C3%B6nskat%20utseende%20och%20funktion)  
* . They’d likely prioritize available items that need minimal work for speed. Shipping to Oslo adds a bit of time but feasible (they operate in Nordics). What can/can’t deliver: They can deliver all furniture categories required. If mid-century style is critical, truly vintage pieces might need more hunting; Yllw might instead simulate the style by mixing pieces from the 1960s they have or refinishing newer pieces to look retro. Cost vs new: Likely 50% or more savings. For example, refurbished designer chairs at \~1/3 new cost  
* [wihlborgs.se](https://www.wihlborgs.se/sv/om-oss/nyheter/hallbar-fastighetsutveckling/minskad-klimatpaverkan-med-aterbruk-av-kontorsmobler/#:~:text=,vd%20och%20grundare%20av%20Soeco)  
* . Overall, Yllw could probably meet \~80-100% of needs on time, with some creative solutions (so score: 4.5/5, “mostly yes”).  
* Rekomo: Partially. Relying on current stock, Rekomo may not have 45 identical bed frames because they focus on office furniture (beds are not typical office furniture). They might have some ex-hotel beds occasionally, but not guaranteed. They could potentially source from partners (e.g., if a hotel liquidation happens, but within 8 weeks that’s risky to plan). Dining chairs (90): quite possible – e.g., they might have a batch of 100 cafeteria chairs or stackable chairs in wood that could suit a trendy restaurant after minor tweaks. They have listed “café furniture” category  
* [rekomo.se](https://www.rekomo.se/?srsltid=AfmBOoqU2ohc2dmqC6KgIBjGOZ1HrsNQYeJkBlUgsBpSFgQwbDEEUow7#:~:text=ARBETSRUM)  
* . Style might be an issue: their inventory skews office functional. But if the boutique vibe can accept some modern corporate furniture, they have it. Desk chairs (45): easily – lots of ergonomic chairs in stock, though those might clash with boutique decor (black mesh chairs in a boutique hotel room?). They might propose alternative like sled-base guest chairs that look nicer, but then comfort suffers. Lobby furniture: Rekomo has sofas and lounge chairs (often corporate lobby style). Could supply items like nice used designer sofas (they sometimes get HAY or similar lounge pieces  
* [place2place.se](https://place2place.se/?srsltid=AfmBOor3Gqj0TYth_bLwfMb2ucUBdZmSoqjsfDxdTpGj5Uvwe4ukeTL7#:~:text=L%C3%A4gg%20i%20varukorg)  
* ). Lead time: Very quick – items are ready-stock. 8 weeks is fine for existing stock. Missing pieces: Bed frames are the biggest gap. Possibly also decorative lighting – Rekomo doesn’t list much in decorative lamps aside from some used office lamps. They might need to complement with new lighting. Cost vs new: Very favorable (their business model is half price or less). The client might need to compromise on design unity, since Rekomo’s stock is diverse. Perhaps a partial solution: get chairs and desks from Rekomo, but source beds elsewhere (new or from a hotel surplus specialist). Score: 3/5 (partial) – can cover seating and casegoods except beds, aesthetic coherence medium.  
* Input/Greenified: Yes (with caveats). Input’s network could likely source 45 bed frames – possibly from a hotel project (Input sometimes handles hotel refurbs, they might have connections to find used beds in storage). If not identical used beds available, they can suggest ex-showroom beds or prototype beds from manufacturers at discount – though those are technically new, it’s a circular approach if they use deadstock. Dining chairs (90): Input can pull from multiple office sites – e.g., maybe 3 different sets of 30 chairs each and then re-finish them uniformly. They also might have a client (like a closed restaurant) offering exactly 100 chairs. Their platform could locate such batches quickly across Sweden. Desk chairs: trivial – they have many. They could even rent these if project is short-term. Lobby furniture: Input can combine reused unique pieces for an eclectic yet cohesive look – e.g., they often have lightly used designer sofas (from corporate lounges) which in a boutique hotel would shine. Lead time: 8 weeks is challenging if items need refurb and cross-border delivery, but Input has scale. They might treat this as a project order, using both Greenified stock and new as backup. Because Input can fill any gap with new furniture to keep schedule (especially critical like beds). They could meet design by reupholstering pieces in matching fabrics (they have services for that  
* [inputinterior.se](https://www.inputinterior.se/tjanster/aterbruk/#:~:text=Renovera%20befintliga%20eller%20begagnade%20m%C3%B6bler,omtapetsering%20eller%20byte%20av%20delar)  
* ). Cost vs new: Likely around 60-70% of cost of buying entirely new, since some items might be sourced brand new if reused ones aren’t found in time (reducing savings). Still substantial CO₂ and cost savings on big items like chairs. Overall: They can meet all needs either through reuse or a hybrid solution; their ability to ensure cohesive design is high (with in-house designers). Score: 4/5 – basically yes, but might involve some new items or higher cost to expedite.  
* Recycling Partner (RP): Partial. RP’s forte is office, so beds are not in their usual inventory. They might have contacts (maybe they liquidated a small hotel or dorm before), but assuming not, they probably cannot supply 45 identical hotel-grade bed frames from stock. They could *manufacture or adapt* something (RP does carpentry repairs, but making 45 beds from scratch in 8 weeks is unlikely). Chairs (90 dining \+ 45 desk): yes, likely. They have many chairs and can refurbish to match style (paint, new upholstery). For a mid-century look, they might take a sturdy 90s wood chair frame and stain it walnut and re-cover in retro fabric – doable within 8 weeks if frames are in stock. Desk chairs: yes but style mismatch as with Rekomo; they might propose simpler upholstered chairs for the writing desks to fit boutique look. Lobby: They often have some sofas; can refurbish vintage finds (their “Remake” line could come into play to create bespoke lobby pieces from reclaimed materials  
* [cirkularasverige.se](https://cirkularasverige.se/aktorer/rp-kontorsinredning/#:~:text=M%C3%B6bler%20tv%C3%A4ttas%20och%20renoveras%20i,av%20n%C3%A5gon%20anledning%20anpassas)  
* ). Lead time: If items require significant refurbishing (e.g., reupholstering 90 chairs), 8 weeks is tight but perhaps manageable if they allocate enough workforce – they have upholstery capacity (Artex partnership) to scale up  
* [artex.se](https://www.artex.se/sv/referenser/hyfer-objects#:~:text=RP%20M%C3%96BLER%20OCH%20INREDNING%20,Vi%20renoverar%20m%C3%B6blerna)  
* . Transport to Oslo adds complexity (import duties, but manageable). Cost vs new: Very good – they pride on cost-effectiveness. Might be a bit higher than self-service options due to the refurb work (but still \~50% cheaper than new high-end boutique furniture). Missing: The bed frames likely need to be new or from another supplier. Score: 3/5 – can partially meet (all seating, tables, etc.) but beds are a gap, and style cohesion would rely on their customization capabilities.  
* Kompanjonen: Partial (or as coordinator). Kompanjonen itself wouldn’t “have” the items, but they can orchestrate sourcing from multiple places. For 45 bed frames – they might quickly reach out through their network (maybe knowing a large hotel that closed or an upcoming demolition of a student housing that had beds). 8 weeks is short for that approach, but not impossible if the timing is lucky. They can broker purchase from one source and transfer to the project. Chairs and other furniture: They can find 90 dining chairs via their network (e.g., knowing that a canteen in a company is closing). They could find desk chairs easily from an office clearance. Lobby items: Possibly search marketplace for retro pieces; or connect with antique dealers. Lead time: The risk is coordination time. 8 weeks might be consumed just arranging deals unless they have ready leads. They *excel at quick inventories* – if the hotel had existing furniture, they’d say “reuse what you have.” But in this scenario, it’s presumably all from external sources. Realistically, Kompanjonen might say: They can supply some items but not all within 8 weeks. They might recommend mixing new and reused to hit timeline (they’ll handle reused parts). Cost: Could be low for items found (maybe they negotiate good deals), but their consulting fee and multiple transport arrangements add overhead. Also, cross-border to Oslo might be an issue (they operate mainly in Sweden – but could collaborate with a Norwegian partner like Loopfront). Score: 2/5 – as a solo supplier, not ideal for urgent full fit-out; however as a *facilitator*, they could complement others.  
* Återbruksfabriken: No (for furniture). They deal with building materials mostly, not furniture, so beds/chairs are outside their scope. They could provide some interior materials if needed (e.g., reclaimed wood panels to build a bar, or reused lighting fixtures if any in stock). For the given needs, they wouldn’t be the go-to. They might partner with a furniture supplier to give a complete offering, but on their own: beds/chairs no, maybe some decorative or construction elements for lobby (like reclaimed flooring). Score: 1/5 for furniture needs; not applicable.  
* Brattöns Återbruk: No for uniform volume. They might have a few cool vintage chairs or some doors/timber for the boutique vibe, but assembling 45 identical of anything is unlikely. They could contribute accent pieces (like maybe 5 unique lobby chairs – eclectic, not matching though). And timeline to get to Oslo adds to impractical. Score: 1/5.  
* Place2Place: Partial. Place2Place’s catalog sometimes has large quantities: e.g., they had 68 matching Fritz Hansen dining chairs listed  
* [place2place.se](https://place2place.se/?srsltid=AfmBOor3Gqj0TYth_bLwfMb2ucUBdZmSoqjsfDxdTpGj5Uvwe4ukeTL7#:~:text=L%C3%A4gg%20i%20varukorg)  
* , which could cover the restaurant need nicely (if style fits). 45 desk/task chairs – they had 45 Humanscale lamps and presumably can source similar volumes of chairs  
* [place2place.se](https://place2place.se/?srsltid=AfmBOor3Gqj0TYth_bLwfMb2ucUBdZmSoqjsfDxdTpGj5Uvwe4ukeTL7#:~:text=L%C3%A4gg%20i%20varukorg)  
* . Bed frames are tricky – rarely appear on their site as it's mostly office/home furniture. Possibly they could locate some via their seller network (maybe 45 used IKEA or Fogia bed frames in one batch?). The aesthetic curation might be labor-intensive: their stock is mixed styles; to find mid-century style in volume might not coincide. Lead time: They can dispatch available items quickly (they operate like an e-commerce shipping out within days). So if the design team is flexible (e.g., chooses from what’s currently available on the site), it can meet 8 weeks easily. If specific style is a must, then they might not have time to source beyond current inventory. Cost: Good deals for what they have (some items new 30-40% of retail). They likely cannot guarantee things like fire treatment or reupholstery in that timeframe – items come as is. For a boutique project, an interior designer might need to reupholster after receiving them, which adds time/cost. Score: 2.5/5 – could fill some categories (dining chairs likely yes, others hit-or-miss) on time, but project would need flexibility.

Summary Scenario 1: The best bets are YLLW Factory and Input (Greenified) who can cover nearly all needs through a combination of stock and custom refurb, within 8 weeks, albeit possibly using a hybrid approach (some new items or expedited refurb)

[wihlborgs.se](https://www.wihlborgs.se/sv/om-oss/nyheter/hallbar-fastighetsutveckling/minskad-klimatpaverkan-med-aterbruk-av-kontorsmobler/#:~:text=Soeco%20har%20kontor%2C%20utst%C3%A4llning%20och,f%C3%A5r%20%C3%B6nskat%20utseende%20och%20funktion)

[yllw.com](https://www.yllw.com/yllw-factory#:~:text=Med%20%C3%B6ver%2065%20000%20%C3%A5terbrukade,och%20smart%20alternativ%20till%20nyproduktion)

. Rekomo and RP can cover seating and tables but not beds, so they’d need to be paired with another supplier for beds. Kompanjonen might serve as a useful partner to fill any specific gaps by brokering unique finds (e.g., sourcing genuine mid-century pieces to mix in for authenticity). A likely optimal solution: YLLW (for bulk furniture) \+ Kompanjonen or a vintage dealer (for a few signature pieces) \+ local new purchase for anything like mattresses or certified beds.

### **Scenario 2: Chain Hotel Renovation in Stockholm – *120 rooms, phased over 16 weeks*.**

Needs: 120 identical bed frames (queen size, durable), 240 nightstands (two per room, matching the beds), 120 TV benches/low dressers, 480 bath towels (matching, high quality), corridor textiles (e.g. carpet runners, artwork for walls). Aesthetic: Standardized chain-hotel look, not high luxury but consistent, fairly modern. Everything must be uniform across 120 rooms. Critical: All furniture must have fire certifications (or be treated) appropriate for hotel use (e.g., BS5852 or EN 13501 where applicable), and documentation should be provided. Timeline: 16 weeks total, delivery in phases to allow wing-by-wing renovation (e.g., deliver 60 rooms worth at week 8, then second 60 at week 16). This scenario emphasizes volume, uniformity, and compliance.

* YLLW Factory: Mostly Yes. While Yllw doesn’t normally stock hundreds of hotel beds, they can approach this in a few ways:  
  * Take-back from another hotel: If any large hotel is closing or rebranding, Yllw could procure 120 used bed frames. Not a common occurrence, but not impossible (could be from a chain’s refurb in another city).  
  * Refurbish office furniture into hotel use: For nightstands/TV benches, Yllw could repurpose storage units or tables from offices, refinishing them uniformly. They have carpentry capabilities to resize or add features.  
  * Manufacture using reclaimed materials: They could build simple nightstand frames from reclaimed wood (Pro2Type line) and perhaps reuse drawers from old cabinets. Given 16 weeks, some manufacturing is feasible, especially for something like nightstands that might not be found easily in identical quantity reused.  
    Bed frames: Possibly a mix approach: use existing bed bases (maybe ex-hospital or military barracks steel frames?) then clad in wood veneer for nicer look. They definitely can supply mattresses? (Usually not reused for hygiene; likely new or supplied by client). We focus on frames: likely metal or wood frames can be reused if structurally sound.  
    Towels (480): Textiles are tricky as second-hand due to hygiene. Yllw deals with furniture, not likely linens. They might skip towels entirely (hotel likely buys new towels). If circular, maybe renting towels from a linen service is an option (which is circular in a service sense). But no reuse supplier keeps large stocks of towels, especially with uniform color and hotel grade. This likely needs to be new or through hospitality linen leasing companies. So probably not delivered by Yllw.  
    Corridor textiles/art: Yllw could source carpets from office projects (carpet tiles or rugs) – but hotels need corridor carpet that meets fire code and heavy wear. Used carpet tiles could be an option (some companies sell barely used carpet squares). They could provide those if aesthetic matches (maybe a neutral pattern). Art/decor: They might have some decorative items, but corridors typically use new art or prints. Possibly Yllw could source second-hand framed prints from an office clearance.  
    Compliance: Yllw would ensure all furniture is either inherently compliant or treated. They can have upholstery fabric on headboards or chairs treated to Crib5 standard by working with fire treatment companies (they are aware of these requirements). They likely can provide EN 1021-1/2 test certificates for upholstery they do (using certified fabrics) and documentation for wood furniture if needed (e.g., that surfaces are fire lacquered or meet Euroclass D for wooden furniture, which is usually fine). Nightstands and TV benches typically not upholstered so just need to be sturdy and maybe meet general quality standards. BVD: If asked, they can provide material declaration, though for reused that often means noting it’s reclaimed wood etc.  
    Phased delivery: Absolutely, Yllw can coordinate storing items and delivering in two batches. They have capacity and trucks.  
    Volume capacity: They have done big office projects (e.g., supplied 30,000 chairs overall in stock  
  * [wihlborgs.se](https://www.wihlborgs.se/sv/om-oss/nyheter/hallbar-fastighetsutveckling/minskad-klimatpaverkan-med-aterbruk-av-kontorsmobler/#:~:text=Infl%C3%B6det%20%C3%A4r%20s%C3%A5%20stort%20att,i%20snitt%2C%20%C3%A4r%20ett%20annat)  
  * ). 120 bed sets is within their capacity if sourced. They might coordinate with a partner for some items (maybe work with a bed manufacturer to incorporate some reused components if needed).  
    Cost: Significant savings – bed frames and casegoods reused would be maybe 30–50% of new cost for a mid-range hotel furniture package.  
    Overall: Yllw could cover furniture pieces (beds, nightstands, TV units, maybe corridor furniture like console tables or mirrors), but linens (towels) they won’t supply. Score (excluding towels): 4/5 – strong for furniture, weak for textiles.  
* Rekomo: Partially.  
  Volume uniformity: Rekomo might have 120 of something like chairs or desks, but 120 identical bed frames is unlikely in their normal stock (again bed frames aren’t typical office furniture). They could try to source from a large dorm or so.  
  Nightstands/TV benches: They might propose repurposing office storage (e.g., small two-drawer pedestal units as nightstands). If they have 240 identical pedestals from a bank HQ, those could be painted and topped with a wood panel to look like nightstands. TV benches could be low office cabinets or credenzas – possible if they have a large batch from a conference center. The aesthetics might be utilitarian unless modified. Rekomo doesn’t do heavy carpentry, so modifications would be minimal.  
  Towels: Rekomo doesn’t deal in linens.  
  Corridor carpet/art: Not typically – they sell some rugs or acoustic panels but not large carpet rolls.  
  Phasing: They can store and deliver in batches, yes (they have warehouses).  
  Compliance: If items are originally office-grade, they are usually decent quality. But fire compliance: wooden furniture from offices isn’t typically fire rated (hotels require e.g. IMO for carpets or certain certification for upholstered seating in public areas). If any upholstery is involved (e.g., a padded headboard or chair in room), Rekomo’s items likely would need retroactive treatment or replacement. Rekomo likely cannot arrange fire treatment themselves; that’s outside their normal service. They also may not provide documentation proactively; a client would have to request and perhaps do extra testing.  
  Volume capacity: They can handle logistics for 120 rooms worth (their inventory size is big).  
  Cost: Very low compared to new hotel furniture (they might achieve the entire set for half or less of new price). But risk is that aesthetics and compliance might not fully satisfy chain standards, requiring additional work.  
  Score: 2.5/5 – can supply bulk furniture with modifications, but likely gaps in compliance (would need external help for fire certs) and cannot handle textiles.  
* Input/Greenified: Yes (almost entirely).  
  Input has advantage of possibly tapping into manufacturers’ overstocks for chain hotel uniformity. For example, they might find a discontinued line of hotel furniture (beds and nightstands) in storage and secure it. Or coordinate a take-back from a hotel chain’s renovation (since this scenario *is* a renovation, perhaps Input could manage the furniture being removed – if in good condition they could refurbish and reuse it in the same hotel or another property).  
  120 beds: Input often works with brands like Kinnarps who have hotel bed products; if a large client had surplus, Input can get those. They could also order new frames from a manufacturer and claim circularity by using reused materials elsewhere (though that’s bending the definition). However, because Input is a full-service provider, they might actually recommend mixing new and reused: e.g., reused headboards and nightstands from a closed hotel, combined with new bed bases for warranty.  
  Casegoods: likely yes – they can source uniform sets (maybe from an office with many similar cabinets, or from a cruise ship refit). If not matching out of the box, they can refinish them all identical. They have the resources to re-laminate or repaint furniture in large batches.  
  Towels: Not their domain, but they could connect the hotel to a textile circular service (like a company that recycles or leases textiles – recall the VarUnik example where a new service for hotel linens exists). Input might have that partnership, or at least incorporate it in the sustainability report. But physically, they wouldn’t supply used towels (hygiene and difficulty to source consistent quality).  
  Corridor: They can source used carpet tiles or remnant rolls; also lots of art gets liquidated from offices (framed prints, etc.), so they could curate each floor’s art from secondary market.  
  Phased execution: Input is used to phased office refits, so yes – they can store furniture and deliver wing by wing, and even help install (they have installation crews).  
  Compliance: Top-notch. They will ensure fire rating for textiles (could send any uncertified fabric to a lab for treatment or choose only certified fabrics in reupholstery). They can provide certificates or documentation (they know the standards and have in-house compliance experts for public tenders). For example, if the hotel needs proof that lounge chairs meet EN16139 (strength) and BS5852 (fire), Input can either supply chairs that originally had those certs or arrange testing for a sample. They might factor in an extra 2-4 weeks for testing one of each item at RISE (they have relationships to get that done if needed, at cost).  
  Volume & lead time: 120 rooms in 16 weeks is manageable. They likely would plan and start refurbishing immediately after contract sign, delivering first batch at 8 weeks easily.  
  Cost: Still significantly less than buying all new hotel furniture, but not dirt cheap: They provide high service, so maybe 60% of new cost. But for chain clients, the appeal might also be sustainability (which chains increasingly prioritize).  
  Score: 4.5/5 – basically yes, except they themselves wouldn’t do towels (they’d say go to a textile service), and possibly some small decor elements might be better new.  
* Recycling Partner (RP): Partial.  
  Beds & matching furniture: Not typical stock. RP might have done a project with a hotel liquidation, but unless they coincidentally have 120 beds, they’d have to source externally. They could coordinate with a liquidation auction – e.g., if a large hotel is selling furniture, RP could step in to buy the lot and refurbish them for this project. 16 weeks might allow that if such an opportunity arises early. If not, RP could manufacture simple items – they have carpentry: 240 identical nightstands could be built from scratch using reclaimed wood from their inventory of desks (e.g., cut-down desk tops as panels). This is plausible if design is simple, but it’s a lot of work for 240 pieces.  
  Uniformity: They can achieve uniform finishes via painting/upholstering.  
  Towels: No (they don’t supply linens).  
  Corridor textiles: Unlikely, aside from maybe second-hand signage or something trivial. Not really their field.  
  Phasing: They can deliver in phases, yes. They’d ensure first 60 rooms done, then second. They need to store the rest which they have space for.  
  Compliance: They might need guidance: They can refurbish furniture to like-new, but ensuring fire safety might require external help. They could partner with a fire treatment service (Artex might do fire-retardant fabric treatment if reupholstering chairs). Documentation may not be readily available unless they specifically test. Their sustainability report indicates focus on environment, but not sure on fire cert. Possibly they have not dealt with a stringent hospitality audit, so this is a gap – hence they'd be learning (Level 2-3).  
  Volume capacity: They have done whole offices, but 120 rooms of identical pieces is a challenge if they don’t find an existing batch. They could split source (e.g., get 60 beds of one model and 60 of another similar model – but that breaks uniformity). This scenario might overstretch them unless they collaborate with another vendor or the client is flexible on some new items.  
  Cost: Good savings if they pull it off, but some costs for custom building or treatment would add.  
  Score: 2.5/5 – significant capability on core furniture, but uniform beds and compliance are weak points.  
* Kompanjonen: As coordinator, potentially Yes (but not sole supplier).  
  Kompanjonen could shine in a *renovation project management* role: since it’s a chain-hotel renovation, they might already be involved in inventorying the old furniture. They could help reuse on-site: e.g., perhaps the existing bed frames can be kept and just modified, or among chain properties, shuffle furniture around. They could also source from multiple places: maybe 60 beds from one closed hotel \+ 60 from another. They have knowledge of demolition schedules (they often know in advance what buildings will be stripped)  
* [byggindustrin.se](https://www.byggindustrin.se/utveckling/hallbarhet/aterbruksexperter-om-marknadens-lycksokare-det-ar-rorigt-dar-ute-nu/#:~:text=%C3%85terbruksexperter%20om%20marknadens%20lycks%C3%B6kare%3A%20%E2%80%9DDet,i%20branschen%20kan%20leda)  
* , which could align to gather needed items. They would treat compliance seriously: might propose to test one reused bed frame for strength or get an engineer’s approval.  
  However, they wouldn’t themselves supply towels or textiles – they’d recommend using a sustainable textile vendor (maybe they know VarUnik’s new hotel linen service from industry news). Corridor carpets, they might suggest using a carpet tile from Interface’s reuse program, etc.  
  Phased: They can coordinate phases meticulously, ensuring minimal downtime. Possibly arrange temporary storage of removed items and bring them back cleaned (if reusing the hotel’s own furniture).  
  Realistically: Kompanjonen might not have physical capacity to deliver 120 sets on their own, but if integrated into the project team, they ensure all parties (furniture suppliers, contractors, etc.) work together to maximize reuse.  
  Score: If acting as project facilitator rather than a supplier: Yes for making it happen. If expected to directly furnish: No (they’d outsource the actual supply to others). So we’ll score in context: 4/5 as a facilitator, 1/5 as a stand-alone vendor.  
* Återbruksfabriken: Yes (for building materials aspect).  
  For the main furniture, no – that’s not their area. But for corridor refurbishment, they could supply reused building components: e.g., doors for 120 rooms (if the hotel wanted reclaimed solid wood doors to replace existing – they might find a batch of similar doors from an office demolition). Or ceiling tiles, light fixtures for corridors, etc. If the renovation includes building work (partition walls, etc.), they can contribute materials. They could also provide documentation for LEED/BREEAM on reused materials which chain hotels might need for certification.  
  But in furniture terms, they’d just complement others.  
  Score focusing on the main needs: 1/5 as furniture supplier, but note they could supply some materials.  
* Place2Place: No for large uniform batches.  
  Their marketplace might occasionally have a bulk lot (like those 68 chairs), but 120 identical beds or casegoods, very unlikely. Towel supply not relevant. They might provide a few items like if someone listed 100 identical side tables – but coordinating the whole package via a marketplace would be a logistics nightmare for the hotel. Possibly could source artwork cheaply (like someone selling 200 framed pictures from an office). But as a primary supplier, not suitable. Score: 1/5.

Summary Scenario 2: The best approach likely involves multiple collaborators:

* Input/Greenified or YLLW to provide the hard furniture (beds, nightstands, TV units) with assured compliance and uniform finish.  
* A textile service for towels (likely new or rental; reuse of towels is rare except perhaps if a closed hotel had barely used stock).  
* Kompanjonen or an internal sustainability manager to oversee reuse targets and documentation.  
  If single-operator: Input is the strongest candidate to cover most aspects and compliance. YLLW is strong on furniture but may need help on textile side.  
  Using Återbruksfabriken for any building material needs (doors, etc.) and Kompanjonen for strategy could yield a very high overall reuse content in the renovation.

### **Scenario 3: Luxury Resort Re-Design near Göteborg – *30 suites, flexible 20-week timeline*.**

Needs: High-end design furniture for suites and common areas, with a *mix-and-match boutique look*. Specifically, a range of unique statement pieces (vintage or designer) – e.g., iconic lounge chairs, art deco coffee tables, ornate mirrors – to give each suite a distinct character. Also, custom refurbishment and reupholstering is expected to tailor fabrics to the resort’s color scheme. Additionally, curated art & décor items for an eclectic, upscale ambiance. Timeline: 20 weeks (ample time for sourcing and customizing). Budget: Willing to pay premium for uniqueness; focus is more on sustainability and uniqueness than on cost-cutting, though still expect reused items to be cost-effective relative to equivalent new designer pieces. This scenario tests curatorial skill, access to rare items, and custom refurb quality.

* YLLW Factory: Yes (strong capabilities).  
  Yllw has a vast network and inventory including “classical design furniture in need of new upholstery or color”  
* [wihlborgs.se](https://www.wihlborgs.se/sv/om-oss/nyheter/hallbar-fastighetsutveckling/minskad-klimatpaverkan-med-aterbruk-av-kontorsmobler/#:~:text=I%20Soecos%20lokaler%20st%C3%A5r%20m%C3%A4ngder,l%C3%A4gre%20pris%20och%20l%C3%A4gre%20klimatp%C3%A5verkan)  
* . They specifically mention giving furniture “character and individuality” in new interiors

* . They then collaborate with skilled craftsmen to fully refurbish and even modify them to fit the resort’s style

* Rekomo: No (not suited).

* [place2place.se](https://place2place.se/?srsltid=AfmBOor3Gqj0TYth_bLwfMb2ucUBdZmSoqjsfDxdTpGj5Uvwe4ukeTL7#:~:text=Fritz%20Hansen%20Soffa%201%20st,186%20250%20kr%2Fst%20inkl%20moms)  
* ), but curation is not their business model. They can’t guarantee an eclectic luxury mix.

Greenified might list items like a Knoll Barcelona chair from a law firm or a Carl Hansen daybed from a CEO’s office. Input could gather those gems (they have contacts in many companies – sometimes they know when a company is discarding expensive designer furniture due to redesign).

*  – a similar concept to a boutique hotel suite.

  RP might have some interesting vintage furniture occasionally (they mention classic design pieces in their inventory sometimes). They have strong upholstery/carpentry skills to transform items in creative ways. They even note combining “inredning som gått ur tiden” (outdated interiors) and adapting them  
* [cirkularasverige.se](https://cirkularasverige.se/aktorer/rp-kontorsinredning/#:~:text=M%C3%B6bler%20tv%C3%A4ttas%20och%20renoveras%20i,av%20n%C3%A5gon%20anledning%20anpassas)  
*  – which suggests creative repurposing.  
  However, they may not have a deep catalogue of iconic design objects ready to go. They could do more of a rustic/upcycled chic style than sourcing specific famous design pieces. If the resort’s luxury aesthetic leans towards *eclectic rustic* (like repurposed wood, bespoke handcrafted items), RP could do well. If it’s more mid-century modern luxe, they might not have enough range.  
  They likely would do well with custom requests: e.g., “We need a large statement conference table for a villa suite” – they could build one from reclaimed parquet flooring or similar. Their flexibility and 20 years experience would help.  
  Art & decor: Not their focus, though they might partner with others or source some decorative elements they come across in liquidations.  
  Score: 3/5 – capable of producing unique upcycled items and refurbishing design furniture if provided, but limited in sourcing truly rare pieces spontaneously.  
* Kompanjonen: As curator/advisor, potentially yes.  
  They know the second-hand market deeply, including auctions, vintage shops, etc. They could be hired as curators to find specific statement pieces the resort desires. For example, if the resort wants an authentic vintage Scandinavian sideboard in each suite, Kompanjonen could search across Sweden’s secondary market to find 30 high-quality ones, then coordinate their purchase and send them to a refurbisher (maybe Yllw or RP) for refinishing.  
  Kompanjonen’s value is connecting to niche suppliers: antique dealers, specialty niche reuse like Genbyg in Denmark for architectural salvage (could provide something like antique doors or lamps), or contacting artists who repurpose materials.  
  They likely relish a project like this because it’s about pushing reuse boundaries creatively.  
  However, as a single entity, they don’t deliver finished furniture – they’d assemble a coalition: e.g., find items, then use a partner to reupholster. With 20 weeks, they could manage that process.  
  Score: 4/5 as a facilitator of unique sourcing (particularly if paired with someone like Yllw or a skilled upholsterer to finish the pieces).  
* Återbruksfabriken: Possibly for decor elements.  
  A luxury resort redesign might incorporate reclaimed architectural elements (like an old oak beam installed as a mantle, or vintage floorboards for a rustic effect). Återbruksfabriken could supply such materials or even certain statement fixtures (an old cast iron bathtub, vintage doors). This adds authenticity. They wouldn’t do furniture, but their items can be part of the décor.  
  If the resort concept is “modern meets heritage”, using some reclaimed building materials from Återbruksfabriken can be a highlight (and they provide provenance stories).  
  They can meet custom requests given time: e.g., if asked for “antique wrought iron gates to use as headboard art”, they might locate some through their salvage network.  
  Score: not directly furnishing but valuable complementary. As an “operator” in this scenario, not scored since they don’t supply furniture.  
* Place2Place: Yes for finding specific pieces (with curation).  
  Their platform sometimes has high-end design items (like a Fritz Hansen sofa for 149k SEK
